       |  /// The power operator (note: NOT bitwise XOR).
       |  /// In order to provide a convenient power operator for all [Number]s, the number library
       |  /// overrides the caret operator.  In Dart the caret operator is ordinarily used
       |  /// for bitwise XOR operations on [int]s.
      1|  @override

      3|          Imaginary(expModulus * sin(scaledPhase))));

       |      throw const NumberException(
       |          'The number library does not support raising a complex number to a complex power');
      1|    } else if (exponent is Imaginary) {
       |      throw const NumberException(
       |          'The number library does not support raising a complex number to an imaginary power');
       |    }

       |    return Double.one;
       |  }

       |  ///     {'d': double value}

      0|    if (m.containsKey('d') && m['d'] is num) {
      0|      return Double.fromMap(m as Map<String, num>);

      0|    if (m.containsKey('i') && m['i'] is int) {
      0|      return Integer.fromMap(m as Map<String, int>);
       |    }

      0|      return Precise.fromMap(m as Map<String, String>);

      0|      return Complex.fromMap(m);
       |    }
      0|    if (m.containsKey('imag') && m is Map<String, Map<String, dynamic>>) {
      0|      return Imaginary.fromMap(m);

       |  }

       |  /// Returns the Number equivalent to [n] having the simplest type that can
       |  /// represent the value (in order):  Integer, Double, Imaginary, or Complex.
       |  /// If [n] is already the most simple type possible, then it will be returned directly.
       |  /// Precise Numbers always remain Precise.
     35|  static Number simplifyType(Number n) {
     65|    if (n is Integer || n is Precise) return n;
     66|    if (n is Double) return n.isInteger ? Integer(n.toInt()) : n;
      8|    if (n is Imaginary) {
     14|      if (n.value is Precise) return n;
     23|      if (n.value.toDouble() == 0) return Integer(0);
     26|      if (n.value.isInteger && n.value is Double) {
      8|        return Imaginary(Integer(n.value.toInt()));
       |      }
       |      return n;
       |    }
      8|    if (n is Complex) {
       |      final realZero =
     38|          n.real.value == 0 && (n.real is! Precise || n.real == Precise.zero);
     40|      final imagZero = n.imag.value.value.toDouble() == 0 &&
     23|          (n.imag.value is! Precise || n.imag.value == Precise.zero);
       |      if (realZero) {
      6|        if (imagZero) return simplifyType(n.real);
     16|        return Imaginary(simplifyType(n.imag.value));
       |      } else if (imagZero) {
     10|        return simplifyType(n.real);
       |      } else {
     12|        final simpleReal = simplifyType(n.real) as Real;
     18|        final simpleImag = simplifyType(n.imag.value);
      6|        if (identical(simpleReal, n.real) &&
     12|            identical(simpleImag, n.imag.value)) return n;
      4|        return Complex(simpleReal, Imaginary(simpleImag));
       |      }
       |    }
       |
       |    return n;
       |  }

       |/// `Precise` represents an arbitrary precision number.
       |///
       |/// It can be used anywhere a `Real` `Number` is used.
       |///
       |/// Arbitrary precision can be used to combat the effects of cumulative rounding errors in circumstances
       |/// where those errors can be significant.
       |///
       |/// This class enables arbitrary precision calculations in both Dart and when transpiled to JavaScript by
       |/// representing numbers as digits that stay within the limitations of the underlying number system.
       |///
       |/// In JavaScript the maximum value of a number, because they are 64-bit floating
       |/// point values, is 2^53, or 9007199254740992, and the maximum number of significant digits as a result is 16.
       |///
       |class Precise extends Real {
       |  /// Constructs an arbitrary precision number from a string.
       |  ///
       |  /// The precision can be limited by providing the maximum number of significant digits
       |  /// (default is 50).
       |  ///
       |  /// Examples:
       |  ///     Precise('12')
       |  ///     Precise('0.1234')
       |  ///     Precise('-12.345')
       |  ///     Precise('1.23456789e-6', sigDigits: 4)
       |  ///
     11|  Precise(String value, {int sigDigits = 50}) {
     11|    _precision = sigDigits;
     22|    final str = value.toLowerCase().trim();
     19|    if (str.startsWith('-')) _neg = true;
     11|    final decimalPointIndex = str.indexOf('.');
     11|    final eIndex = str.indexOf('e');
       |
     22|    if (decimalPointIndex != -1) {
     30|      _power = eIndex != -1
      3|          ? -(eIndex - decimalPointIndex - 1)
     40|          : -(str.length - decimalPointIndex - 1);
       |    }
     22|    if (eIndex != -1) {
      5|      _power += int.parse(str.substring(eIndex + 1));
       |    }
     45|    final endParseIndex = eIndex != -1 ? eIndex - 1 : value.length - 1;
       |    var char = '';
       |    var decimalPoint = false;
     33|    for (var index = endParseIndex; index > -1; index--) {
     11|      char = str[index];
       |
       |      // Ignore one decimal.
     11|      if (char == '.') {
       |        if (!decimalPoint) {
       |          decimalPoint = true;
       |          continue;
       |        } else {
      0|          throw Exception(
       |              'Precise cannot parse a string with multiple decimal points');
       |        }
       |      }
       |
       |      // Ignore sign character at start
     22|      if (char == '-' || char == '+' && index == 0) break;
     33|      _digits.add(Digit.char(char));
       |    }
       |
     11|    _trimLeadingZeros();
     11|    _limitPrecision();
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Constructs a Precise number equal to [value].
       |  /// The number of significant digits defaults to 19 for integers and
       |  /// 15 for doubles but may be specified.
     10|  factory Precise.num(num value, {int? sigDigits}) {
     20|    if (value.isNaN || value.isInfinite) {
      0|      throw Exception('Precise value must be a valid finite number');
       |    }
     10|    var precision = sigDigits ?? (value is int ? 19 : 15);
     20|    return Precise(value.toString(), sigDigits: precision);
       |  }

       |  /// Constructs a Precise number, applying the values found in map [m].
       |  /// See `toJson` for the expected format.
      0|  factory Precise.fromMap(Map<String, String>? m) {
      0|    if (m == null) return Precise.zero;
      0|    return Precise(m['precise'] ?? '0');
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Creates a arbitrary precision number directly from digits.
       |  ///
       |  /// [digits] must be ordered from least significant to most.
       |  ///
       |  /// [power] sets the offset of the decimal point, if any (defaults to 0).  For example,
       |  /// a power of -2 means that the decimal point is located between the second and third digits.
       |  /// A power of +2 means that two zeroes are implied before the least significant digit (that is, the number is
       |  /// one hundred times greater than the number specified by the digits).
       |  ///
       |  /// For a negative number set [neg] to true.
       |  ///
       |  /// The default precision is 50 significant digits.
      7|  Precise.raw(List<Digit> digits,
       |      {int power = 0, bool neg = false, int sigDigits = 50}) {
      7|    _precision = sigDigits;
      7|    if (digits.isNotEmpty) {
     14|      _digits.addAll(digits);
       |    } else {
      6|      _digits.add(Digit.zero);
       |    }
      7|    _power = power;
      7|    _neg = neg;
      7|    _precision = sigDigits;
       |
      7|    _trimLeadingZeros();
      7|    _limitPrecision();
       |
       |    // Avoid negative zero.
     44|    if (_neg && _digits.length == 1 && _digits.first == Digit.zero) {
      2|      _neg = false;
       |    }
       |  }

       |  /// Zero as a Precise number.
     24|  static final Precise zero = Precise('0');

      3|  static final Precise one = Precise('1');

       |  /// The digits of the arbitrary precision number are represented as a list of Digit objects,
       |  /// lowest significant digit to most significant digit.
       |  final List<Digit> _digits = <Digit>[];
       |
       |  /// The offset of the decimal point.
     16|  int get power => _power;
       |  int _power = 0;
       |
       |  /// Flag for negative values.
       |  bool _neg = false;

       |  /// Optional precision cutoff (maximum number of significant digits allowed).
     14|  int get precision => _precision;

      7|  set precision(int? sigDigits) {
      7|    _precision = sigDigits ?? 50;
      7|    _limitPrecision();
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Returns a copy of the internal digits list, from least significant to most.
     30|  List<Digit> get digits => List<Digit>.from(_digits);
       |
       |  /// If the specified precision is lower than the number of digits,
       |  /// truncates the digits and adjusts the power accordingly.
       |  /// Rounds the least significant digit based on the
       |  /// most significant truncated digit.
     11|  void _limitPrecision() {
     44|    if (_digits.length > _precision) {
      8|      final numCull = _digits.length - _precision;
       |      var roundUp = false;
       |
       |      // Round based on the digit one past the max precision
      6|      for (var i = numCull - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
      4|        final d = _digits.removeAt(i);
      8|        if (i == numCull - 1 && d.toInt() > 4) roundUp = true;
       |      }
      4|      _power += numCull;
       |
       |      if (roundUp) {
      4|        if (_digits[0] == Digit.nine) {
       |          var i = 0;
      7|          while (i < _digits.length && _digits[i] == Digit.nine) {
      3|            _digits[i] = Digit.zero;
      1|            i++;
       |          }
       |
      3|          if (i == _digits.length) {
       |            // Carry the 1.
      3|            _digits.add(Digit.one);
      2|            _digits.removeAt(0);
      2|            _power++;
       |          } else {
      7|            _digits[i] = Digit(_digits[i].toInt() + 1);
       |          }
       |        } else {
      8|          _digits[0] = Digit.list[_digits[0].toInt() + 1];
       |        }
       |      }
       |    }
       |  }

       |  /// Returns the digit at [place], where place is with respect to the decimal number system
       |  /// (that is, place 1 is tens, place 2 is hundreds, place -3 is thousandths, etc).
       |  ///
       |  /// Therefore place is not a direct index into the digits list; power must be taken into account first.
       |  ///
      8|  Digit digitAtPlace(int place) {
     16|    final index = place - power;
     40|    if (index > -1 && index < _digits.length) {
     16|      return _digits[index];
       |    } else {
      7|      return Digit.zero;
       |    }
       |  }

       |  /// Returns true if the stored value can be represented exactly as an integer.
     11|  @override
       |  bool get isInteger {
     22|    if (_power >= 0) return true;
       |
       |    // Check for case where decimal portion is equal to 0
     80|    for (final d in digits.sublist(0, min(digits.length, _power.abs()))) {
     20|      if (d != Digit.zero) return false;
       |    }
       |    return true;
       |  }

      1|  @override

       |  /// Return only the decimal portion as a Precise number.

       |  /// 0.4567.  An integer value will return [zero].
      1|  Precise get decimalPortion {

      2|        power: _power, neg: _neg);

       |  /// Addition operator.
       |  /// The precision of the product is the lesser of the precision of the two
       |  /// numbers so as not to imply a level of accuracy not present in the inputs.
      7|  @override
       |  Precise operator +(dynamic addend) {
      7|    final preciseAddend = toPrecise(addend);
       |
     21|    var targetPrecision = min(_precision, preciseAddend.precision);
       |
       |    // Divert to subtraction if signs are not the same
     21|    if (_neg != preciseAddend._neg) {
     13|      if (_neg) return preciseAddend - (-this);
      2|      return this - (-preciseAddend);
       |    }
       |
      7|    final placeExtents = determinePlaceExtents(this, preciseAddend);
      7|    final sum = <Digit>[];
       |    var carry = 0;
       |    var temp = 0;
     28|    for (var place = placeExtents[0]; place <= placeExtents[1]; place++) {
      7|      final d1 = digitAtPlace(place);
      7|      final d2 = preciseAddend.digitAtPlace(place);
     14|      temp = (d1 + d2) + carry;
      7|      if (temp < 10) {
     21|        sum.add(Digit.list[temp]);
       |        carry = 0;
       |      } else {
     12|        sum.add(Digit.list[temp - 10]);
       |        carry = 1;
       |      }
       |    }
       |
     11|    if (carry == 1) sum.add(Digit.one);
       |
      7|    return Precise.raw(sum,
     14|        power: placeExtents[0], neg: _neg, sigDigits: targetPrecision);
       |  }

       |  /// Subtraction operator.
       |  /// The precision of the difference is the lesser of the precision of the two
       |  /// numbers so as not to imply a level of accuracy not present in the inputs.
      6|  @override
       |  Precise operator -(dynamic subtrahend) {
      6|    final preciseSubtrahend = toPrecise(subtrahend);
       |
     18|    final targetPrecision = min(_precision, preciseSubtrahend.precision);
       |
       |    // Divert to addition if signs are different
     18|    if (_neg != preciseSubtrahend._neg) {
      4|      if (_neg) return -(preciseSubtrahend + (-this));
      2|      return this + (-preciseSubtrahend);
       |    }
       |
       |    // Flip operation if subtrahend is greater
     22|    if (preciseSubtrahend.abs() > abs()) return -(preciseSubtrahend - this);
       |
       |    // Subtrahend is lesser; safe to borrow
      6|    final placeExtents = determinePlaceExtents(this, preciseSubtrahend);
      6|    final diff = <Digit>[];
       |    var borrow = 0;
       |    var temp = 0;
     24|    for (var place = placeExtents[0]; place <= placeExtents[1]; place++) {
      6|      final d1 = digitAtPlace(place);
      6|      final d2 = preciseSubtrahend.digitAtPlace(place);
     12|      temp = (d1 - d2) + borrow;
      6|      if (temp < 0) {
     24|        diff.add(Digit.list[10 + temp]);
      6|        borrow = -1;
       |      } else {
     18|        diff.add(Digit.list[temp]);
       |        borrow = 0;
       |      }
       |    }
       |
      6|    return Precise.raw(diff,
     12|        power: placeExtents[0], neg: _neg, sigDigits: targetPrecision);
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Multiplication operator.
       |  /// The precision of the product is the lesser of the precision of the two
       |  /// numbers so as not to imply a level of accuracy not present in the inputs.
      7|  @override
       |  Precise operator *(dynamic multiplier) {
      7|    final preciseMultiplier = toPrecise(multiplier);
       |
       |    // Target precision of the product.
     21|    var targetPrecision = min(_precision, preciseMultiplier.precision);
       |
       |    // Provide some headroom for the calculation.
     14|    preciseMultiplier.precision += 5;
       |
      7|    var product = Precise.zero;
      7|    var intermediateProduct = <Digit>[];
     21|    final combinedPower = _power + preciseMultiplier._power;
       |    var carry = 0;
       |    var temp = 0;
       |    var offset = 0;
      7|    for (var p1 = preciseMultiplier._power;
     35|        p1 < preciseMultiplier._power + preciseMultiplier._digits.length;
      7|        p1++) {
     14|      final d1Int = preciseMultiplier.digitAtPlace(p1).toInt();
      7|      intermediateProduct = <Digit>[];
     49|      for (var p2 = _power; p2 < _power + _digits.length; p2++) {
      7|        final d2 = digitAtPlace(p2);
     21|        temp = (d1Int * d2.toInt()) + carry;
       |
      7|        if (temp < 10) {
     21|          intermediateProduct.add(Digit.list[temp]);
       |          carry = 0;
       |        } else {
      5|          carry = temp ~/ 10;
     25|          intermediateProduct.add(Digit.list[temp - (carry * 10)]);
       |        }
       |      }
      7|      if (carry != 0) {
     15|        intermediateProduct.add(Digit.list[carry]);
       |        carry = 0;
       |      }
       |
     12|      for (var i = 0; i < offset; i++) {
     10|        intermediateProduct.insert(0, Digit.zero);
       |      }
       |
     14|      product += Precise.raw(intermediateProduct,
     28|          sigDigits: max(_precision, preciseMultiplier.precision) + 5);
      7|      offset += 1;
       |    }
       |
     14|    return Precise.raw(product._digits,
     14|        power: combinedPower + product.power,

       |  /// Division operator.
       |  /// The precision of the product is the lesser of the precision of the two
       |  /// numbers so as not to imply a level of accuracy not present in the inputs.
      4|  @override
       |  Number operator /(dynamic divisor) {
      4|    var preciseDivisor = toPrecise(divisor);
       |
       |    // Target precision of the quotient.
     12|    var targetPrecision = min(_precision, preciseDivisor.precision);
       |
       |    // Headroom.
      8|    preciseDivisor.precision += 5;
       |
     12|    final negResult = _neg != preciseDivisor._neg;
       |
      8|    if (preciseDivisor == Precise.zero) {
      6|      if (this == Precise.zero) return Double.NaN;
       |      return negResult ? Double.negInfinity : Double.infinity;
       |    }
      8|    if (preciseDivisor == Precise('1')) return this;
       |
       |    // Use the absolute value of the divisor from here
      4|    preciseDivisor = preciseDivisor.abs();
       |
       |    // Shift of decimal place
       |    var shift = 0;
      8|    if (preciseDivisor._power < 0) {
      8|      shift = -preciseDivisor._power;
       |
       |      // Convert divisor to integer
      8|      preciseDivisor = Precise.raw(preciseDivisor.digits);
       |    }
       |
       |    // Long division algorithm
      8|    final divisorDigits = preciseDivisor._digits.length;
       |    //int remainder = 0;
      4|    final result = <Digit>[];
     12|    var digitCursor = _digits.length - 1;
      4|    var temp = <Digit>[];
     12|    while (result.length < _precision) {
       |      // If into bonus digits and remainder is 0, done
      4|      if (digitCursor < 0) {
     12|        if (Precise.raw(temp) == Precise.zero) {
       |          break;
       |        }
       |      }
       |
       |      // Process next digit
     20|      temp.insert(0, digitCursor >= 0 ? _digits[digitCursor] : Digit.zero);
      8|      if (digitCursor < 0) shift--;
      8|      if (temp.length >= divisorDigits) {
      4|        final p = Precise.raw(temp);
      4|        if (p >= preciseDivisor) {
       |          // Find the highest multiple of the divisor that is less than p
     12|          for (var i = 9; i > -1; i--) {
      4|            if (i == 0) {
      0|              result.insert(0, Digit.zero);
       |              break;
       |            }
       |
      4|            final prod = preciseDivisor * i;
      4|            if (prod <= p) {
     12|              result.insert(0, Digit.list[i]);
       |
       |              // Remainder is temp
     12|              temp = List<Digit>.from((p - prod)._digits);
       |
       |              break;
       |            }
       |          }
       |        } else {
      8|          result.insert(0, Digit.zero);
       |        }
       |      } else {
      8|        if (result.isNotEmpty) result.insert(0, Digit.zero);
       |      }
      4|      digitCursor--;
       |    }
       |
      4|    return Precise.raw(result,
      8|        power: power + shift, neg: negResult, sigDigits: targetPrecision);
       |  }

      1|  @override

      2|        for (var i = 1; i < exp; i++) {

       |        }
       |        return p;
       |      }

       |    }
       |  }

       |  /// Converts a num, Number or String into a Precise object.
       |  /// int and Integer precision defaults to 19.
       |  /// double and Double precision defaults to 15.
       |  /// Any other kind of object defaults to 50.
       |  /// The precision parameter can override these defaults.
       |  /// If obj is a Precise object, a copy will be returned and its
       |  /// precision will be transferred unless overridden.
      7|  static Precise toPrecise(dynamic obj, {int? desiredPrecision}) {
      7|    if (obj is Precise) {
     21|      return Precise('$obj', sigDigits: desiredPrecision ?? obj.precision);
       |    }

     10|    if (obj is num) return Precise.num(obj, sigDigits: desiredPrecision ?? 15);

     10|      return Precise.num(obj.toInt(), sigDigits: desiredPrecision ?? 19);
       |    }
      4|    if (obj is Number) {
      8|      return Precise.num(obj.toDouble(), sigDigits: desiredPrecision ?? 15);
       |    }

       |  /// The truncating division operator.
       |  /// When dividing by an [Imaginary] or [Complex] number, the result will contain an imaginary component.
       |  /// The imaginary component is *not* truncated; only the real portion of the result is truncated.
      3|  @override

       |  /// The modulo operator.
       |  /// [Imaginary] and [Complex] divisors are nor supported and will throw an Exception.
      0|  @override
       |  Number operator %(dynamic divisor) {
      0|    if (divisor is num) return Double((value % divisor).toDouble());
      0|    if (divisor is Real) return Double((value % divisor.value).toDouble());
      0|    if (divisor is Complex || divisor is Imaginary) {
      0|      throw Exception(
       |          'Unsupported operation (% with imaginary or complex divisor)');
       |    }
       |    // Treat divisor as 0
       |    return Double.NaN;
       |  }
       |
       |  /// The power operator (note: NOT bitwise XOR).
       |  ///
       |  /// In order to provide a convenient power operator for all [Number]s, the number library
       |  /// overrides the caret operator.  In Dart the caret operator is ordinarily used
       |  /// for bitwise XOR operations on [int]s.  The [Integer] class provides the `bitwiseXor` method
       |  /// as a substitute.
     14|  @override
       |  Number operator ^(dynamic exponent) {
     14|    if (exponent is num) {
     28|      final raised = pow(value, exponent);
     56|      if (raised.toInt() == raised) return Integer(raised.toInt());
      6|      return Double(raised as double);
       |    }
      0|    if (exponent is Precise) return (Precise.num(value)) ^ exponent;
      0|    if (exponent is Real) {
      0|      final raised = pow(value, exponent.value);
      0|      if (raised.toInt() == raised) return Integer(raised.toInt());
      0|      return Double(raised.toDouble());
       |    }
      0|    if (exponent is Complex) {
       |      // a^(b+ic) = a^b * ( cos(c * ln(a)) + i * sin(c * ln(a)) )
      0|      final coeff = this ^ exponent.real;
      0|      final clna = (exponent.imaginary.value * log(value)).toDouble();
      0|      return Complex(coeff * cos(clna) as Real, Imaginary(coeff * sin(clna)));
       |    }
      0|    if (exponent is Imaginary) {
       |      // a^(ic) = cos(c * ln(a)) + i * sin(c * ln(a))
      0|      final clna = (exponent.value * log(value)).toDouble();
      0|      return Complex(cos(clna) as Real, Imaginary(sin(clna)));
       |    }
       |    return Double.one;
       |  }
       |
     26|  @override
       |  bool operator >(dynamic obj) {
     76|    if (obj is num) return value > obj;
     17|    if (obj is Precise) return Precise.num(value) > obj;
     32|    if (obj is Real) return value > obj.value;
      9|    if (obj is Imaginary) return value > 0;
      9|    if (obj is Complex) return this > obj.real;
      0|    return this > 0;
       |  }
       |
     10|  @override
     19|  bool operator >=(dynamic obj) => this == obj || this > obj;
       |
      8|  @override
      8|  bool operator <(dynamic obj) => !(this >= obj);
       |
     25|  @override
     25|  bool operator <=(dynamic obj) => !(this > obj);

     14|      : value is int

     28|          : Double(value.abs().toDouble());

      7|  @override
       |  Number reciprocal() {
     14|    if (value == 0) return Double.NaN;
     14|    final num flipped = 1.0 / value;
     14|    return flipped.toInt() == flipped
      6|        ? Integer(flipped.toInt())
     12|        : Double(flipped.toDouble());
       |  }

       |        ? divisor
      0|        : divisor is Number
      0|            ? divisor.toDouble()
       |            : 0;

      4|    if (rem is int) return Integer(rem);
      4|    return Double(rem.toDouble());
       |  }

C:\dev\github\quantity\lib\src\number\util\erf.dart
       |import 'dart:math';
       |
       |/// Approximate solution for the error function of [x].
       |///
       |/// * Fractional error is less than 1.2e7.
       |/// * There is no standard erf() available in dart:math.
       |/// * The approximation is based on Chebyshev fitting.
       |///
      1|double erf(double x) {
      1|  final z = x.abs();
      3|  final t = 1.0 / (1.0 + 0.5 * z);
       |
       |  // Approximate the complementary error function
      1|  var erfc = t *
      4|      exp(-z * z -
      1|          1.26551223 +
      1|          t *
      1|              (1.00002368 +
      1|                  t *
      1|                      (0.37409196 +
      1|                          t *
      1|                              (0.09678418 +
      1|                                  t *
      2|                                      (-0.18628806 +
      1|                                          t *
      1|                                              (0.27886807 +
      1|                                                  t *
      2|                                                      (-1.13520398 +
      1|                                                          t *
      1|                                                              (1.48851587 +
      1|                                                                  t *
      2|                                                                      (-0.82215223 +
      1|                                                                          t * 0.17087277)))))))));
       |
      2|  if (x < 0.0) erfc = 2.0 - erfc;
      1|  return 1.0 - erfc;
       |}
C:\dev\github\quantity\lib\src\number\util\jenkins_hash.dart
       |/// Generates a unique hash for a set of objects.
      7|int hashObjects(Iterable<Object> objects) {
       |  var hash = 0;
     14|  for (final obj in objects) {
     21|    hash = 0x1fffffff & (hash + obj.hashCode);
     28|    hash = 0x1fffffff & (hash + ((0x0007ffff & hash) << 10));
     14|    hash = hash ^ (hash >> 6);
       |  }
     28|  hash = 0x1fffffff & (hash + ((0x03ffffff & hash) << 3));
     14|  hash = hash ^ (hash >> 11);
     28|  return 0x1fffffff & (hash + ((0x00003fff & hash) << 15));
       |}

       |/// Create a [MutableQuantity] with the same value, dimensions and uncertainty as [q].
      0|MutableQuantity toMutable(Quantity q) => MutableQuantity()..setEqualTo(q);
       |
       |/// MutableQuantity supports updates to its value, dimensions and uncertainty.
       |/// Changes are broadcast over the `onChange` stream.
       |///
       |/// ## Inversion
       |/// The Quantity class supports inversion through the `inverse`
       |/// method, which returns a Quantity object that is the result of the
       |/// inversion process.  MiscQuantity adds to this capability with the
       |/// `invert` method, which inverts the MiscQuantity in place without
       |/// returning a object.  This is possible because a MiscQuantity may have
       |/// any Dimensions, whereas other Quantity subclasses have fixed Dimensions.
       |// ignore: avoid_implementing_value_types
       |class MutableQuantity implements Quantity {
       |  /// Constructs an instance, with optional SI-MKS value, dimensions and/or relative uncertainty.
      1|  MutableQuantity(
       |      [this._valueSI = Double.zero,
       |      this._dimensions = Scalar.scalarDimensions,
       |      this._ur = 0.0]);
       |
       |  /// Constructs an instance from an existing Quantity.
      1|  MutableQuantity.from(Quantity q)
      1|      : _valueSI = q.valueSI,
      1|        _dimensions = q.dimensions,
      1|        _ur = q.relativeUncertainty,
      1|        preferredUnits = q.preferredUnits;
       |
       |  // Value.
      1|  @override
      1|  Number get valueSI => _valueSI;
       |  Number _valueSI;
      1|  set valueSI(dynamic value) {
      2|    if (value != _valueSI) {
      2|      if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
      2|      _valueSI = objToNumber(value);
      3|      _onChange.add(snapshot);
       |    }
       |  }
       |
       |  // Dimensions.
      1|  @override
      1|  Dimensions get dimensions => _dimensions;
       |  Dimensions _dimensions;
      1|  set dimensions(Dimensions dim) {
      2|    if (dim != _dimensions) {
      2|      if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
      1|      _dimensions = dim;
       |
       |      // Any preferred units will no longer be valid.
      1|      preferredUnits = null;
       |
      3|      _onChange.add(snapshot);
       |    }
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Relative uncertainty.
       |  double _ur = 0;
       |
      1|  @override
      1|  double get relativeUncertainty => _ur;
       |
       |  /// Sets the relative standard uncertainty in this Quantity object's value.
       |  ///
       |  /// - Will throw an ImmutableQuantityException if this Quantity is in an immutable state.
       |  /// - Relative standard uncertainty is defined as the standard uncertainty
       |  ///   divided by the absolute value of the quantity.  Standard uncertainty, in turn,
       |  ///   is defined as the uncertainty (of a measurement result) by an estimated
       |  ///   standard deviation, which is equal to the positive square root of the
       |  ///   estimated variance.  One standard deviate in a Normal distribution
       |  ///   corresponds to a coverage factor of 1 (k=1) and a confidence of approximately 68%.
      1|  set relativeUncertainty(double value) {
      2|    if (value != _ur) {
      2|      if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
      1|      _ur = value;
      3|      _onChange.add(snapshot);
       |    }
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Preferred units for display.
       |  @override
       |  Units? preferredUnits;
       |
       |  /// Mutability can be turned on and off (defaults to true).
       |  bool mutable = true;
       |
       |  /// Broadcasts a snapshot of quantity whenever its value, dimensions or uncertainty changes.
      3|  Stream<Quantity> get onChange => _onChange.stream;
       |  final StreamController<Quantity> _onChange =
       |      StreamController<Quantity>.broadcast();
       |
      1|  @override
      1|  Number get mks => valueSI;
       |
       |  /// Sets the [value] of this quantity in standard MKS (meter-kilogram-second) units.
      1|  set mks(Number value) {
      2|    if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
      3|    if (value != valueSI) valueSI = value; // valueSI send the change event
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Creates and returns an immutable typed [Quantity] that represents the value and
       |  /// uncertainty of this MutableQuantity at this moment.
      3|  Quantity get snapshot => dimensions.toQuantity(
      6|      preferredUnits?.fromMks(valueSI) ?? valueSI, preferredUnits, _ur);
       |
      0|  @override
      0|  Number get cgs => snapshot.cgs;
       |
       |  /// Sets the value of this quantity in alternative CGS (or centimeter-gram-second) units.
       |  /// MKS (meter-kilogram-second) units are preferred.
       |  ///
       |  /// - Although CGS units were once commonly used and contended for the role
       |  /// of standard units, their use is now discouraged in favor of the adopted
       |  /// standard MKS (or meter-kilogram-second) units.
       |  /// - Throws an ImmutableQuantityException if this Quantity has been made immutable.
       |  ///
       |  /// See [set mks(double)].
      1|  set cgs(Number value) {
      2|    if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
       |
       |    var val = value;
       |
       |    // Adjust for centimeters vs. meters.
      2|    final lengthExp = dimensions.getComponentExponent(Dimensions.baseLengthKey);
      3|    val /= pow(100.0, lengthExp.toDouble());
       |
       |    // Adjust for grams vs. kilograms.
      2|    final massExp = dimensions.getComponentExponent(Dimensions.baseMassKey);
      3|    val /= pow(1000.0, massExp.toDouble());
       |
      3|    mks = Double(val.toDouble());
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Modifies this MutableQuantity to have the value, dimensions, uncertainty and
       |  /// preferred units of [q2].
      1|  Quantity setEqualTo(Quantity q2) {
      2|    if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
       |
      2|    preferredUnits = q2.preferredUnits;
       |
      3|    if (valueSI != q2.valueSI ||
      0|        _dimensions != q2.dimensions ||
      0|        _ur != q2.relativeUncertainty) {
      2|      _valueSI = q2.valueSI;
      2|      _dimensions = q2.dimensions;
      2|      _ur = q2.relativeUncertainty;
      3|      _onChange.add(snapshot);
       |    }
       |
       |    return this;
       |  }
       |
      0|  @override
      0|  Quantity sqrt() => snapshot.sqrt();
       |
      0|  @override
      0|  Quantity get standardUncertainty => snapshot.standardUncertainty;
       |
       |  /// Sets the relative standard uncertainty in this Quantity object's value to [su].
       |  ///
       |  /// * Will throw an ImmutableQuantityException (a RuntimeException) if this
       |  /// Quantity is in an immutable state.
       |  /// * Relative standard uncertainty is defined as the standard uncertainty
       |  /// divided by the absolute value of the quantity.  Standard uncertainty, in turn,
       |  /// is defined as the uncertainty (of a measurement result) by an estimated
       |  /// standard deviation, which is equal to the positive square root of the
       |  /// estimated variance.  One standard deviate in a Normal distribution
       |  /// corresponds to a coverage factor of 1 (k=1) and a confidence of approximately 68%.
      1|  set standardUncertainty(Quantity su) {
      2|    if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
      3|    if (!(dimensions == su.dimensions)) {
      1|      throw DimensionsException(
       |          'The standard uncertainty must have the same dimensions as this Quantity object');
       |    }
       |
       |    // Determine ur.
      1|    final ratio = su / this; // Scalar
      3|    _ur = ratio.mks.toDouble();
      3|    _onChange.add(snapshot);
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Sets the this Quantity's [value] in the specified [units]. The [value] is expected to
       |  /// be a num or Number object.  The [units] must match the current [dimensions] or a
       |  /// [DimensionsException] will be thrown.
      1|  void setValueInUnits(dynamic value, Units units) {
      2|    if (!mutable) throw ImmutableQuantityException(q: this);
       |
       |    // Check for compatible dimensions.

       |/// Represents a range of quantity values.
       |class QuantityRange<Q extends Quantity> {
       |  /// Constructs a quantity range, from [q1] to [q2].
      4|  QuantityRange(this.q1, this.q2);
       |
       |  /// The starting quantity of the range.
       |  Q q1;
       |
       |  /// The ending quantity of the range.
       |  Q q2;
       |
       |  // Derived values (calculated on first use)
       |  Q? _minValue;
       |  Q? _maxValue;
       |  Q? _centerValue;
       |  Q? _span;
       |
       |  /// The minimum value in this range.
      9|  Q get minValue => _minValue ??= (q1.valueSI <= q2.valueSI) ? q1 : q2;
       |
       |  /// The maximum value in this range.
      9|  Q get maxValue => _maxValue ??= (q1.valueSI > q2.valueSI) ? q1 : q2;
       |
       |  /// The value at the center of the range.
      0|  Q get centerValue => _centerValue ??= (q1 + q2) / 2.0 as Q;
       |
       |  /// The magnitude of the range.
       |  /// This value is always positive (or zero).  Get [delta] for the signed version of the range.
      0|  Q get span => _span ??= (q2 - q1).abs() as Q;
       |
       |  /// The change in value from start to end, which may be negative.
      0|  Q get delta => q2 - q1 as Q;
       |
       |  /// Returns true if this range overlaps [range2]
       |  /// (exclusive of the endpoints).
      0|  bool overlaps(QuantityRange<Q> range2) {
      0|    if (range2.minValue <= minValue) {
      0|      return range2.maxValue > minValue;
       |    } else {
      0|      return range2.minValue < maxValue;
       |    }
       |  }
       |
       |  /// True if this range contains [quantity], with a tolerance, [epsilon], of
       |  /// rounding errors of 1.0e-10 and [inclusive] of the endpoints by default.
      1|  bool contains(Q quantity, [bool inclusive = true, double epsilon = 1.0e-10]) {
      4|    if (inclusive && (quantity == q1 || quantity == q2)) return true;
      1|    if (epsilon == 0.0) {
      4|      if (q1 < quantity && q2 > quantity) return true;
      4|      if (q1 > quantity && q2 < quantity) return true;
       |    } else {
       |      if (inclusive) {
      5|        if (q1.mks - epsilon < quantity.mks &&
      5|            q2.mks + epsilon > quantity.mks) {
       |          return true;
       |        }
      5|        if (q1.mks + epsilon > quantity.mks &&
      5|            q2.mks - epsilon < quantity.mks) {
       |          return true;
       |        }
       |      } else {
      5|        if (q1.mks - epsilon <= quantity.mks &&
      5|            q2.mks + epsilon >= quantity.mks) return true;
      5|        if (q1.mks + epsilon >= quantity.mks &&
      0|            q2.mks - epsilon <= quantity.mks) return true;
       |      }
       |    }
       |    return false;
       |  }

      0|  bool encompasses(QuantityRange<Q> range2) =>
      0|      (minValue <= range2.minValue) && (maxValue >= range2.maxValue);

       |/// The Dimensions class represents the dimensions of a physical quantity.
       |///
       |/// ## The Seven Base Quantities
       |/// In the International System of Units (SI) all quantities are considered
       |/// to be either one of the seven base quantities (Length, Mass, Time Interval,
       |/// Temperature, Current, Intensity and Amount of Substance) or derived from
       |/// those base quantities through combinations and/or arbitrary exponents.
       |/// The Dimensions of a quantity capture which combination applies for that
       |/// particular quantity.  Any combination of these base quantities is possible;
       |/// in practice less than 100 derived quantities are in common use.
       |/// The Dimensions of a quantity determine its type and directly relate to that
       |/// quantity's significance and meaning in the real world.
       |///
       |/// ## The Dimensions Class Also Tracks Angle and Solid Angle
       |/// The dimensions that are tracked include the seven base SI quantities and
       |/// also the angle and solid angle dimensionless quantities.  Angular
       |/// quantities are often distinguished from their non-angular counterparts
       |/// even if the SI base dimensions are equal.  Consequently, in order
       |/// to support such differentiation, Angle and SolidAngle dimensions are stored
       |/// alongside the base seven dimensions and used to distinguish between
       |/// dimensions and determine quantity types.  To test whether two Dimensions
       |/// objects are equal strictly in terms of the base SI dimensions, the
       |/// equalsSI method may be used.
       |class Dimensions {
       |  /// No-arg constructor sets all dimensions to zero (that is, a scalar quantity).
      1|  Dimensions()
      1|      : _dimensionMap = <String, num>{},
       |        qType = Scalar;
       |
       |  /// Constructs a constant Dimensions object with a map of base dimension keys to exponents
   7834|  const Dimensions.constant(Map<String, num> dims, {this.qType})
       |      : _dimensionMap = dims;
       |
       |  /// Constructs a Dimensions object with a map of base dimension keys to base dimension exponents.
      6|  Dimensions.fromMap(Map<String, num> typeValuePairs)
      6|      : _dimensionMap = Map<String, num>.from(typeValuePairs),
       |        qType = null;
       |
       |  /// Creates a Dimensions object by copying an existing Dimensions object.
       |  ///
       |  /// This is a deep copy that clones the internal _dimensionMap HashMap
       |  /// object (which in turn contains only immutable objects of classes String and num).
       |  ///
       |  /// Any type hint is preserved by default but can be cleared by setting `includeTypeHint` to false.
      5|  Dimensions.copy(Dimensions d2, {bool includeTypeHint = true})
     10|      : _dimensionMap = Map<String, num>.from(d2._dimensionMap),
      1|        qType = includeTypeHint ? d2.qType : null;
       |
       |  /// The dimensions (base dimension key -> base dimension exponent)
       |  final Map<String, num> _dimensionMap;
       |
       |  // DIMENSION COMPONENTS
       |
       |  // ==basic SI dimensions==
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: Length
       |  static const String baseLengthKey = 'Length';
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: Mass
       |  static const String baseMassKey = 'Mass';
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: Time Interval
       |  static const String baseTimeKey = 'Time';
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: Temperature
       |  static const String baseTemperatureKey = 'Temperature';
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: Current
       |  static const String baseCurrentKey = 'Current';
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: (Luminous) Intensity
       |  static const String baseIntensityKey = 'Intensity';
       |
       |  /// Identifier for Base SI Quantity: Amount of Substance
       |  static const String baseAmountKey = 'Amount';
       |
       |  // ==special derived==

       |  /// Returns an instance of the Quantity type associated with these dimensions.
       |  /// If no specific Quantity type is found with dimensions that match these dimensions
       |  /// an instance of the [MiscQuantity] class will be returned.
       |  /// If no [value] is provided, it defaults to zero.

       |  /// If no uncertainty is provided, the value is presumed to be exact.
     11|  Quantity toQuantity(
       |      [dynamic value = 0.0, Units? units, double uncert = 0.0]) {
       |    // Check that the units match the dimensions, if provided.
     19|    if (units is Quantity && (units as Quantity).dimensions != this) {
      0|      throw DimensionsException(
       |          'The dimensions of the provided units must equal the dimensions');
       |    }
       |    try {
     17|      final type = qType ?? determineQuantityType(this);
     11|      if (type is! MiscQuantity) {
     11|        return createTypedQuantityInstance(type, value, units, uncert: uncert);
       |      }
       |    } catch (e) {
       |      // Ignore.
       |
       |      // This can happen during intermediate equation calculations, for example when
       |      // an element in a divisor is inverted to a miscellaneous type in preparation
       |      // for multiplication.  Since it's not really a problem, log at the finest level.
       |    }
       |
       |    // Unable to create a typed instance; return a MiscQuantity with these dimensions.
      4|    return MiscQuantity(units?.toMks(value) ?? value, this, uncert);
       |  }

       |/// A version of scientific notation in which the exponent of ten must be divisible by
       |/// three (e.g., 123.345 x 10^3).
       |class EngineeringFormatSI extends NumberFormatSI {
       |  /// Constructs an instance.
      1|  EngineeringFormatSI({super.unicode});
       |
       |  /// Move the decimal point.
      1|  @override
       |  String adjustForExponent(String str) {
      2|    if (str.isNotEmpty != true) return str;
      1|    var trimmed = str.trim();
       |    var sign = '';
      1|    if (trimmed.startsWith('-')) {
       |      sign = '-';
      1|      trimmed = trimmed.substring(1);
      1|    } else if (trimmed.startsWith('+')) {
      0|      trimmed = trimmed.substring(1);
       |    }
       |
      1|    final dotIndex = trimmed.indexOf('.');
      2|    final eIndex = trimmed.toLowerCase().indexOf('e');
       |
      1|    var firstNonZeroDigit = -1;
      3|    for (var i = 0; i < trimmed.length; i++) {
      1|      final s = trimmed[i];
      4|      if (s != '0' && s != '.' && s != '-' && s != '+') {
       |        firstNonZeroDigit = i;
       |        break;
       |      }
       |    }
       |
      2|    if (firstNonZeroDigit == -1) return '0.0';
       |
       |    final includedExponent =
      5|        eIndex != -1 ? num.parse(trimmed.substring(eIndex + 1)) : 0;
       |
      3|    final length = eIndex != -1 ? eIndex : trimmed.length;
      5|    var exp = (dotIndex == -1 ? length - 1 : dotIndex - firstNonZeroDigit) +
       |        includedExponent;
      2|    if (dotIndex > firstNonZeroDigit) exp--;
       |
      7|    final num effExp = exp < 0 ? ((exp + 1) ~/ 3) * 3 - 3 : (exp ~/ 3) * 3;
      2|    final adj = (exp - effExp).floor();
       |
      2|    var engStr = eIndex != -1
      1|        ? trimmed.substring(firstNonZeroDigit, eIndex)
      1|        : trimmed.substring(firstNonZeroDigit);
      3|    if (engStr.length == 1 && firstNonZeroDigit < dotIndex) {
      0|      engStr = '$engStr.0';
       |    } else {
       |      // Insert the decimal point after the first non zero digit.
      1|      engStr = engStr.replaceAll('.', '');
      5|      if (engStr.length < adj + 1) engStr = engStr.padRight(adj + 1, '0');
      5|      engStr = '${engStr.substring(0, adj + 1)}.${engStr.substring(adj + 1)}';
      2|      if (engStr.endsWith('.')) engStr = '${engStr}0';
       |    }
       |
      1|    engStr = NumberFormatSI.removeInsignificantZeros(engStr);
       |
       |    // Prepend the sign.
      1|    engStr = '$sign$engStr';
       |
       |    // Append the exponent.
      1|    if (effExp != 0) {
      1|      engStr = unicode
      1|          ? '$engStr \u{00d7} 10${unicodeExponent(effExp)}'
      2|          : '$engStr x 10^$effExp';
       |    }
       |
       |    return engStr;
       |  }

       |/// NumberFormatSI implements the International System of Units (SI) style
       |/// conventions for displaying values of quantities.  Specifically:
       |///
       |/// - Three-digit groups of numbers with more than four digits are separated
       |/// by spaces instead of commas (for example, 299 792 458, not
       |/// 299,792,458) to avoid confusion with the decimal marker in European
       |/// literature.  This spacing is also used to the right of the decimal
       |/// marker (for example, 12 345.678 90).
       |/// - Uncertainty in the quantity's value may be optionally displayed...
       |/// e.g., 1.234(11) or 1.234 +/- 0.011.
       |///
       |/// The value will be displayed in "computer scientific notation" (e.g., 1.3E9)
       |/// if its exponent is less than -3 or greater than 6.  These thresholds are
       |/// arbitrary, but track with typical usage.  If the exponent does not pass one
       |/// of these thresholds then the number is simply displayed as a normal
       |/// decimal number (e.g., 1 234.567 89).
       |///
       |/// The standard DecimalFormat class is unable to apply grouping to digits
       |/// after the decimal.  Therefore, this class directly extends NumberFormat
       |/// and provides implementations for format and parse.
       |class NumberFormatSI implements NumberFormat {

       |  bool unicode;

     34|        realStr = number.toInt().toString();

      0|      } else if (number is Precise) {

      2|          ..write('i')
      4|          ..write(s.substring(expIndex));
       |      }
       |    }
       |
     19|    return buf.toString();
       |  }

       |  /// Looks for the start of an exponent section.
     19|  int _exponentIndex(String str) {
     19|    var expIndex = str.indexOf(' x 10');
     57|    if (expIndex == -1) expIndex = str.indexOf(' \u{00d7} 10');
     57|    if (expIndex == -1) expIndex = str.indexOf('E');
     57|    if (expIndex == -1) expIndex = str.indexOf('e');

       |  /// Returns a String with spaces added according to SI guidelines.
     19|  String insertSpaces(String str) {
       |    // Remove any exponent piece and add it back in after spaces are added.
     19|    final expIndex = _exponentIndex(str);
     44|    final numStr = expIndex != -1 ? str.substring(0, expIndex) : str;
       |
     19|    final decimalIndex = numStr.indexOf('.');
     53|    final preCount = decimalIndex != -1 ? decimalIndex : numStr.length;
     80|    final postCount = decimalIndex != -1 ? numStr.length - decimalIndex - 1 : 0;
       |
     19|    final buf = StringBuffer();
       |
       |    // Pre-decimal.
     19|    if (preCount > 4) {
       |      final preStr =
      8|          decimalIndex != -1 ? numStr.substring(0, decimalIndex) : numStr;
      6|      final fullGroups = preStr.length ~/ 3;
      9|      var cursor = preStr.length - fullGroups * 3;
      9|      if (cursor != 0) buf.write(preStr.substring(0, cursor));
      9|      while (cursor + 3 <= preStr.length) {
      9|        if (cursor != 0) buf.write(unicode ? '\u{2009}' : ' ');
      9|        buf.write(preStr.substring(cursor, cursor + 3));
      3|        cursor += 3;
       |      }
       |    } else {
     38|      if (decimalIndex != -1) {
     26|        buf.write(numStr.substring(0, decimalIndex));
       |      } else {
     15|        buf.write(numStr);
       |      }
       |    }
       |
       |    // Decimal and post-decimal.
     38|    if (decimalIndex != -1) {
     14|      buf.write('.');
     14|      if (postCount > 4) {
       |        // Insert a space after each grouping of 3.
     44|        buf.write(numStr.substring(decimalIndex + 1, decimalIndex + 4));
       |        var cursor = 3;
     11|        while (cursor < postCount) {
       |          buf
     22|            ..write(unicode ? '\u{2009}' : ' ')
     44|            ..write(numStr.substring(decimalIndex + 1 + cursor,
     44|                min(decimalIndex + 4 + cursor, numStr.length)));
     11|          cursor += 3;
       |        }
       |      } else {
     21|        buf.write(numStr.substring(decimalIndex + 1));
       |      }
       |    }
       |
     50|    if (expIndex != -1) buf.write(str.substring(expIndex));
       |
     19|    return buf.toString();
       |  }

       |  /// Removes any zeros at the end of a number string that follow a decimal
       |  /// point (except for one that immediately follows the decimal point).
      4|  static String removeInsignificantZeros(String str) {
       |    try {
      8|      if (str.isNotEmpty != true) return str;
      4|      final dotIndex = str.indexOf('.');
      8|      if (dotIndex == -1) return str;
      8|      final eIndex = str.toLowerCase().indexOf('e');
       |      final decimalCount =
     22|          eIndex == -1 ? str.length - dotIndex - 1 : eIndex - dotIndex - 1;
      4|      if (decimalCount < 2) return str;
     17|      final lastDigitIndex = eIndex == -1 ? str.length - 1 : eIndex - 1;
       |      int endIndex;
     11|      for (endIndex = lastDigitIndex; endIndex > dotIndex + 1; endIndex--) {
     12|        if (str.substring(endIndex, endIndex + 1) != '0') break;
       |      }
      8|      return eIndex == -1
      8|          ? str.substring(0, endIndex + 1)
      4|          : '${str.substring(0, endIndex + 1)}${str.substring(eIndex)}';
       |    } catch (e, s) {
      0|      logger.severe('Problem removing insignificant zeros', e, s);
       |      return str;
       |    }
       |  }

      3|  String _normalizeText(String text) {
       |    // Replace spaces, unicode chars and exponential notation before parsing.
       |    var adj = text
      3|        .replaceAll(' ', '')
      3|        .replaceAll('\u{2009}', '')
      3|        .replaceAll('x10^', 'E')
      3|        .replaceAll('x10', 'E');
      6|    for (final char in expUnicodeMap.keys) {
      3|      final unicodeChar = expUnicodeMap[char]!;
      3|      adj = adj.replaceAll(unicodeChar, char);
       |    }
       |    return adj;
       |  }

       |import 'dart:math' as math;
       |import 'package:intl/intl.dart';
       |import 'package:quantity/quantity.dart';
       |
       |/// The abstract base class for all quantities.  The Quantity class represents
       |/// the value of a physical quantity and its
       |/// associated dimensions.  It provides methods for constructing and getting the
       |/// quantity's value in arbitrary units, methods for mathematical manipulation
       |/// and comparison and optional features such as arbitrary precision and uncertainty.
       |///
       |/// ## Definitions
       |/// _from [NIST's introduction to the International System of Units](http://physics.nist.gov/cuu/Units/introduction.html)_
       |///
       |/// * A _quantity in the general sense_ is a property ascribed to phenomena,
       |/// bodies, or substances that can be quantified for, or assigned to, a
       |/// particular phenomenon, body, or substance.  Examples are mass and electric
       |/// charge.
       |/// * A _quantity in the particular sense_ is a quantifiable or assignable
       |/// property ascribed to a particular phenomenon, body, or substance.  Examples
       |/// are the mass of the moon and the electric charge of the proton.
       |/// * A _physical quantity_ is a quantity that can be used in the mathematical
       |/// equations of science and technology.
       |/// * A _unit_ is a particular physical quantity, defined and adopted by
       |/// convention, with which other particular quantities of the same kind
       |/// (dimension) are compared to express their value.
       |/// * The _value of a physical quantity_ is the quantitative expression of a
       |/// particular physical quantity as the product of a number and a unit, the
       |/// number being its numerical value.  Thus, the numerical value of a particular
       |/// physical quantity depends on the unit in which it is expressed.
       |///
       |/// ## Immutable
       |/// Quantity instances are immutable; they may not be changed after creation.
       |/// Use `MutableQuantity` in the quantity_ext library for situations where
       |/// changing a Quantity object's value or units is required.
       |///
       |/// ## Value Representation,  Arbitrary Precision
       |/// Quantity supports values specified by [num] or [Number] objects.  `Number` subtypes
       |/// include [Real], [Imaginary] and [Complex].  Various [Real] subtypes are
       |/// available, including [Precise], which supports arbitrary precision calculations.
       |///
       |/// ## Uncertainty
       |/// A Quantity object optionally includes an uncertainty, as quantities are
       |/// often determined by measurement and therefore are only accurate within
       |/// the capabilities of the measuring devices or techniques.  Internally,
       |/// the uncertainty of a quantity is modeled as a Normal (Gaussian) distribution.
       |/// The shape of this 'bell curve' distribution is captured by a single value:
       |/// the relative standard uncertainty.  This method of expressing uncertainty is
       |/// used for all physical constants and is accepted for general use with all
       |/// quantities (because quantities, as measurable entities, all follow the same
       |/// logic for representing the uncertainty generated by the combination of
       |/// values from many different experiments).  The relative standard uncertainty
       |/// corresponds to an approximately 68% confidence level that the quantity's
       |/// value is in the stated range.  For different confidence levels, alternative
       |/// coverage factors may be used (k=2 ~95%; k=3 ~99%).  Uncertainty calculations
       |/// may be switched on or off as desired.  It is automatically on if the Quantity
       |/// is constructed with any uncertainty and off otherwise.  The setCalcUncertainty
       |/// method may be called at any point to enable/disable this capability.
       |abstract class Quantity implements Comparable<dynamic> {
       |  /// This constructor sets the [value] (as expressed in the accompanying units)
       |  /// and the relative standard uncertainty.  The value is may be set using any
       |  /// `num` or `Number` object, including [Precise] for arbitrary precision.
       |  ///
       |  /// Both the value and the uncertainty default to zero.
       |  ///
       |  /// Quantity dimensions are derived from the [preferredUnits] and default to scalar
       |  /// dimensions if units are not provided.
       |  ///
       |  /// Relative standard uncertainty is defined as the standard uncertainty
       |  /// divided by the absolute value of the result.  Standard uncertainty, in turn,
       |  /// is defined as the uncertainty (of a measurement result) by an estimated
       |  /// standard deviation, which is equal to the positive square root of the
       |  /// estimated variance.  One standard deviate in a Normal distribution
       |  /// corresponds to a coverage factor of 1 (k=1) and a confidence of approximately 68%.
     86|  Quantity(
       |      [dynamic value = Integer.zero, this.preferredUnits, double uncert = 0.0])
     86|      : valueSI = preferredUnits?.toMks(value ?? 0) ??
      0|            (value is Number ? value : numToNumber(value as num)),
     86|        dimensions = (preferredUnits is Quantity)
     86|            ? (preferredUnits as Quantity).dimensions
       |            : Scalar.scalarDimensions,
       |        _ur = uncert;
       |
       |  /// Used to construct a constant Quantity.
   1963|  const Quantity.constant(
       |      this.valueSI, this.dimensions, this.preferredUnits, this._ur);
       |
       |  /// A constructor to support miscellaneous quantities:  dimensions are known, units are not.
     89|  Quantity.misc(
       |      [dynamic value = 0.0, Dimensions? dimensions, double uncert = 0.0])
     89|      : valueSI = (value is num)
     82|            ? numToNumber(value)
     67|            : value is Number
       |                ? value
       |                : Integer.zero,
       |        dimensions = dimensions ?? Scalar.scalarDimensions,
       |        preferredUnits = null,
       |        _ur = uncert;
       |
       |  /// The value of the quantity in the [base units](http://physics.nist.gov/cuu/Units/current.html),
       |  /// of the International System of Units (SI).
       |  ///
       |  /// This is often referred to as the _MKS_ value to highlight that the units reference meters
       |  /// and kilograms rather than centimeters and grams (_CGS_) as was often done before standardization.
       |  /// The [mks] getter offers a shorthand way to retrieve this value.
       |  final Number valueSI;
       |
       |  /// Dimensions.
       |  final Dimensions dimensions;
       |
       |  /// Sets whether or not uncertainty is to be calculated within mathematical methods.
       |  // bool calcUncertainty = false;
       |
       |  /// The relative standard uncertainty.
       |  final double _ur;
       |
       |  /// Preferred units for display.
       |  final Units? preferredUnits;
       |
       |  ///  Whether or not this Quantity is represented using arbitrary precision.
       |  ///
       |  /// The values of arbitrarily precise Quantities are stored internally as
       |  /// [Precise] Number objects.
       |  ///
       |  /// Arbitrary precision calculations will generally be
       |  /// significantly slower than limited precision (double) calculations because
       |  /// arbitrary precision calculations typically occur in software while
       |  /// double precision calculations often are accelerated directly in hardware.
      0|  bool get arbitraryPrecision => valueSI is Precise;
       |
       |  /// Whether or not this Quantity has scalar dimensions, including having no angle or
       |  /// solid angle dimensions.
       |  ///
       |  /// Use `isScalarSI` to see if these Dimensions are scalar in the strict
       |  /// International System of Units (SI) sense, which allows non-zero angular and
       |  /// solid angular dimensions.
     24|  bool get isScalar => dimensions.isScalar;
       |
       |  /// Whether or not this Quantity has scalar dimensions in the strict
       |  /// International System of Units (SI) sense, which allows non-zero angle and
       |  /// solid angle dimensions.
       |  ///
       |  /// Use `isScalarSI` to see if these Dimensions are scalar in the strict
       |  /// International System of Units sense, which allows non-zero angular and
       |  /// solid angular dimensions.
      0|  bool get isScalarSI => dimensions.isScalarSI;
       |
       |  /// The relative standard uncertainty in this Quantity object's value.
       |  ///
       |  /// Relative standard uncertainty is defined as the standard uncertainty
       |  /// divided by the absolute value of the quantity.  Standard uncertainty, in turn,
       |  /// is defined as the uncertainty (of a measurement result) by an estimated
       |  /// standard deviation, which is equal to the positive square root of the
       |  /// estimated variance.  One standard deviate in a Normal distribution
       |  /// corresponds to a coverage factor of 1 (k=1) and a confidence of approximately 68%.
    154|  double get relativeUncertainty => _ur;
       |
       |  /// Returns the expanded uncertainty for coverage factor, [k], in this
       |  /// Quantity's value as a typed Quantity object.
       |  ///
       |  /// * The expanded uncertainty is defined as a multiple of the standard
       |  /// uncertainty and may be used when the 68.27% confidence represented by the
       |  /// standard uncertainty (k=1) is not adequate.
       |  /// * Confidence values (i.e., the percentage of the distribution encompassed)
       |  /// for other values of the coverage factor 'k' include:
       |  ///
       |  /// 1. 90% for k=1.645,
       |  /// 2. 95.45% for k=2,
       |  /// 3. 99% for k=2.576 and
       |  /// 4. 99.73% for k=3.
      1|  Quantity calcExpandedUncertainty(double k) =>
      7|      dimensions.toQuantity(valueSI.abs() * _ur * k);
       |
       |  /// Returns the standard uncertainty in this Quantity object's value as a typed
       |  /// Quantity object.
       |  ///
       |  /// Standard uncertainty
       |  /// is defined as the uncertainty (of a measurement result) by an estimated
       |  /// standard deviation, which is equal to the positive square root of the
       |  /// estimated variance.  One standard deviate in a Normal distribution
       |  /// corresponds to a coverage factor of 1 (k=1) and a confidence of approximately
       |  /// 68%.

     12|      dimensions.toQuantity(valueSI.abs() * _ur);

       |  /// Randomly generates a Quantity from this Quantity's value and uncertainty.
       |  /// The uncertainty is represented by a Normal (Gaussian) continuous
       |  /// distribution.
       |  ///
       |  /// Because the uncertainty is represented by the continuous normal
       |  /// distribution there are no upper or lower limits on the value that this
       |  /// method will return.
       |  ///
       |  /// If the relative uncertainty is zero, then this Quantity will be returned.
      1|  Quantity randomSample() {
      2|    if (_ur == 0.0) return this;
       |
       |    // Generate a random number btw 0.0 and 1.0
      2|    final rand = math.Random().nextDouble();
       |
      2|    final test = 2.0 * rand - 1.0;
       |
       |    // Iterate on erf until we get a close enough match
       |    var delta = 1.0;
       |    const eps = 0.0001;
      1|    var x = -4.0;
       |    var count = 0;
      1|    while (count < 10000) {
      1|      final fx = erf(x);
      3|      if ((fx - test).abs() < eps) {
      2|        final z = x * math.sqrt(2.0);
      3|        return this + (standardUncertainty * z);
       |      }
       |
       |      // Reverse direction and halve it if past it
      1|      if (fx > test) {
      1|        x -= delta; // backtrack... went too far
      1|        delta *= 0.5; // take smaller steps
       |      } else {
      1|        x += delta;
       |      }
       |
      1|      count++; // safety valve
       |    }
       |
       |    // just in case
       |    return this;
       |  }

       |  /// Calculates the relative combined uncertainty resulting from the addition or
       |  /// subtraction of two Quantities.
     11|  static double calcRelativeCombinedUncertaintySumDiff(
       |      Quantity q1, Quantity q2, Number valueSI) {
     42|    if (q1._ur != 0.0 || q2._ur != 0.0) {
       |      // Standard uncertainties (derived from relative standard uncertainties).
      5|      final u1 = q1._ur * q1.valueSI.abs().toDouble();

      4|      final uc = math.sqrt(u1 * u1 + u2 * u2);

      3|      return uc / valueSI.abs().toDouble();
       |    }

       |    return 0;
       |  }

       |/// Formats a number as a single integer digit, followed by decimal digits
       |/// and raised to a power of 10 (e.g., 1.2345 x 10^3).
       |class ScientificFormatSI extends NumberFormatSI {
       |  /// Constructs an instance.
      2|  ScientificFormatSI({super.unicode});
       |
       |  /// Move the decimal point to just after the first integer digit.
      2|  @override
       |  String adjustForExponent(String str) {
      4|    if (str.isNotEmpty != true) return str;
      2|    var trimmed = str.trim();
       |    var sign = '';
      2|    if (trimmed.startsWith('-')) {
       |      sign = '-';
      1|      trimmed = trimmed.substring(1);
      2|    } else if (trimmed.startsWith('+')) {
      0|      trimmed = trimmed.substring(1);
       |    }
       |
      2|    final dotIndex = trimmed.indexOf('.');
      4|    final eIndex = trimmed.toLowerCase().indexOf('e');
       |
      2|    var firstNonZeroDigit = -1;
      5|    for (var i = 0; i < trimmed.length; i++) {
      2|      final s = trimmed[i];
      4|      if (s != '0' && s != '.') {
       |        firstNonZeroDigit = i;
       |        break;
       |      }
       |    }
       |
      4|    if (firstNonZeroDigit == -1) return '0.0';
       |
       |    final includedExponent =
      7|        eIndex != -1 ? num.parse(trimmed.substring(eIndex + 1)) : 0;
       |
      6|    final length = eIndex != -1 ? eIndex : trimmed.length;
      9|    var exp = (dotIndex == -1 ? length - 1 : dotIndex - firstNonZeroDigit) +
       |        includedExponent;
      4|    if (dotIndex > firstNonZeroDigit) exp--;
       |
      4|    var sciStr = eIndex != -1
      1|        ? trimmed.substring(firstNonZeroDigit, eIndex)
      2|        : trimmed.substring(firstNonZeroDigit);
      4|    if (sciStr.length == 1) {
      1|      sciStr = '$sciStr.0';
       |    } else {
       |      // Insert the decimal point after the first non zero digit.
      2|      sciStr = sciStr.replaceAll('.', '');
      6|      sciStr = '${sciStr[0]}.${sciStr.substring(1)}';
       |    }
       |
      2|    sciStr = NumberFormatSI.removeInsignificantZeros(sciStr);
       |
       |    // Prepend the sign.
      2|    sciStr = '$sign$sciStr';
       |
       |    // Append the exponent.
      2|    if (exp != 0) {
      2|      sciStr = unicode
      2|          ? '$sciStr \u{00d7} 10${unicodeExponent(exp)}'
      3|          : '$sciStr x 10^$exp';
       |    }
       |
       |    return sciStr;
       |  }

       |import '../../number.dart';

       |/// A unit is a particular physical quantity, defined and adopted by
       |/// convention, with which other particular quantities of the same kind
       |/// (dimensions) are compared to express their value.
       |///
       |/// The Units class represents a unit and includes a name (plural), an optional
       |/// intermediate abbreviation, an optional symbol and an optional singular form.
       |/// A Units object stores a conversion value (to convert a value to SI-MKS units)
       |/// and dimensions.
       |///
       |/// ## Abstract Units Mixin
       |/// This class is designed to be used as a mixin.  In this way typed units
       |/// wind up being quantities themselves, extending the associated quantity type
       |/// and mixing in units to represent themselves as units objects (e.g.,
       |/// `LengthUnits extends Length with Units`).  This is
       |/// consistent with the definition of units as quantities with specific values
       |/// and means also that units objects _are quantity objects_ and can be used
       |/// as quantity parameters.
       |///
       |/// ## 'Units' vs. 'Unit'
       |/// Precisely speaking, quantities are expressed as multiples of a particular
       |/// unit (singular, not plural).  However, when the quantity's absolute value is
       |/// greater than 1, the unit is pluralized when spoken.  For example, one says
       |/// 'five meters,' not 'five of the meter unit' or something along those lines.
       |/// Therefore, to make units easier to work with and program, this package calls
       |/// this class Units and not Unit and defines all static
       |/// unit objects with plural names (e.g., _meters_ vs. _meter_).  This leads to a
       |/// more natural expression upon Quantity object creation and value manipulation.
       |mixin Units {
       |  /// The name of the units (plural).
       |  late String name;
       |
       |  /// The name of the units in singular form.
       |  late String singular;
       |
       |  /// The primary abbreviation for the units.
       |  String? abbrev1;
       |
       |  /// A secondary abbreviation for the units.
       |  String? abbrev2;
       |
       |  /// Multiply by this value to convert a Quantity in these units to SI-MKS units.
       |  late Number convToMKS;
       |
       |  /// Whether these units are considered a base metric unit.
       |  bool metricBase = false;
       |
       |  /// The offset of this unit from zero in the metric unit scale.
       |  double offset = 0;
       |
       |  /// The Type to which the Units apply
       |  Type get quantityType;
       |
       |  /// Two units are considered equal if their conversions to MKS are equal and
       |  /// they have the same singular name.
     77|  @override
       |  bool operator ==(Object obj) {
       |    if (identical(this, obj)) return true;
       |
      0|    if (obj is Units) {
      0|      return singular == obj.singular && convToMKS == obj.convToMKS;
       |    }
       |    return false;
       |  }

       |  /// then the singular version of the name will be returned.

     16|      abbrev2 ?? abbrev1 ?? (sing ? singular : name);

       |  /// Calculates and returns the value in SI-MKS units of the specified [value]
       |  /// (that is implicitly in these units).
       |  /// The method expects [value] to be a num or Number object; any other type will
       |  /// cause a [QuantityException].
    203|  Number toMks(dynamic value) {
    245|    if (value is num || value is Number) {
       |      Number term;
    203|      if (value is Precise) {
       |        // Preserve the Precise value's precision.
       |        var preciseConv =
     15|            Precise(convToMKS.toString(), sigDigits: value.precision + 1);
      3|        term = preciseConv * value;
      6|        if (offset == 0) return term;
      0|        return term +
      0|            Precise(offset.toString(), sigDigits: value.precision + 1);
       |      } else {
    406|        term = convToMKS * value;
    406|        if (offset == 0) return term;
     15|        return term + objToNumber(offset);
       |      }
       |    } else {
       |      throw const QuantityException('num or Number expected');
       |    }
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Calculates and returns the value in the units represented by this Units
       |  /// object of [mks] (that is expected to be in SI-MKS units).
       |  /// The method accepts a num or Number object; any other type will
       |  /// cause a [QuantityException].
     21|  Number fromMks(dynamic mks) {
     21|    if (mks is num) {
      2|      if (offset == 0) return Double(mks.toDouble()) / convToMKS;
      7|      return (Double(mks.toDouble()) / convToMKS) - objToNumber(offset);
     21|    } else if (mks is Number) {
     82|      if (offset == 0) return mks / convToMKS;
     10|      return (mks / convToMKS) - objToNumber(offset);
       |    } else {
       |      throw const QuantityException('num or Number expected');
       |    }
       |  }

       |/// A planar (2-dimensional) angle, which has dimensions of _1_ and is a
       |/// measure of the ratio of the length of a circular arc to its radius.
       |///
       |/// Example usage:
       |///
       |///     // Construct an Angle in radians.
       |///     var ang = Angle(rad: 1.1);
       |///
       |///     // Construct an Angle in degrees.
       |///     var ang2 = Angle(deg: 270);
       |///
       |///     // Find the difference.
       |///     var diff = ang2 - ang;
       |///
       |///     // Display the result in degrees.
       |///     print(diff.valueInUnits(Angle.degrees));
       |///
       |/// See the [Wikipedia entry for Angle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angle)
       |/// for more information.
       |class Angle extends Quantity {

       |  /// Optionally specify a relative standard uncertainty.
      3|  Angle({dynamic rad, dynamic deg, double uncert = 0.0})
      8|      : super(deg ?? (rad ?? 0.0), deg != null ? Angle.degrees : Angle.radians,
       |            uncert);
       |
       |  /// Constructs an instance without preferred units.
     18|  Angle.misc(dynamic conv) : super.misc(conv, Angle.angleDimensions);

       |  /// Constructs an Angle based on the [value]
       |  /// and the conversion factor intrinsic to the passed [units].
       |  ///
       |  /// Unlike other Quantity subclasses, the Angle constructor requires
       |  /// both value _and units_ to be provided.  This is to avoid any confusion
       |  /// between radians and degrees, which is a common source of programming
       |  /// errors.
       |  ///
       |  /// The dimension is set to the static [angleDimensions] parameter.
       |  ///
       |  /// The internal value is automatically bounded between -PI and PI
       |  /// radians (-180 to 180 degrees)

      0|      : super.constant(valueSI, Angle.angleDimensions, units, uncert);
       |

       |  ///  passed in for degrees, minutes, and seconds of arc.
      0|  Angle.fromDegMinSec(int d, int m, double s, [double uncert = 0.0])
      0|      : super(degrees.toMks(d) + minutesArc.toMks(m) + secondsArc.toMks(s),
      0|            Angle.radians, uncert);

      0|  static final AngleUnits minutesArc = AngleUnits('arc minutes', '\'',
       |      'arc min', 'arc minute', const Double.constant(2.9088821e-4), false);
       |

      0|  static final AngleUnits secondsArc = AngleUnits('arc seconds', '\'',
       |      'arc sec', 'arc second', const Double.constant(4.8481368e-6), false);

      0|  static final AngleUnits minutes = minutesArc;

       |  /// Accepted for use with the SI; equivalent to [secondsArc].
      0|  static final AngleUnits seconds = secondsArc;

       |  /// Return an equivalent angle bounded to between -PI and PI
       |  /// (-180 and 180 degrees).
       |  /// If this Angle is already within that range then it is returned directly.
      0|  Angle get angle180 {
      0|    if (valueSI >= -math.pi && valueSI <= math.pi) return this;
       |
      0|    var rad = valueSI.toDouble();
      0|    while (rad < -math.pi) {
      0|      rad += twoPi;
       |    }
      0|    while (rad > math.pi) {
      0|      rad -= twoPi;
       |    }
      0|    return Angle(rad: rad);
       |  }
       |
       |  /// Returns an equivalent angle bounded to between 0 and 2PI
       |  /// (0 and 360 degrees).
       |  /// If this Angle is already within that range then it is returned directly.
      2|  Angle get angle360 {
      8|    if (valueSI >= 0.0 && valueSI <= twoPi) return this;
      4|    var rad = valueSI.toDouble();
      2|    rad = rad.remainder(twoPi);
      6|    if (valueSI < 0) rad += twoPi;
      2|    return Angle(rad: rad);

       |  /// Calculates the cosine of this angle.
      0|  double cosine() => math.cos(mks.toDouble());

       |  /// Calculates the sine of this angle.
      0|  double sine() => math.sin(mks.toDouble());
       |

      0|  double tangent() => math.tan(mks.toDouble());

       |  /// Calculates and returns the secant of this angle.

      0|  double secant() => 1.0 / math.cos(mks.toDouble());

       |  /// Calculates and returns the cosecant of this angle.

      0|  double cosecant() => 1.0 / math.sin(mks.toDouble());

      0|  double cotangent() => 1.0 / math.tan(mks.toDouble());
